Hangzhou Municipal Government Prevents

Japanese Students from Visiting the Mainland

Shirai Ko, the Japanese Consul stationed in Hangzhou, stated that students from the Dongwen College were scheduled to come to Hangzhou this month and visit Ningbo, Shaoxing, and other places. Yesterday, he specifically met with Zhao Zhiyou, the Mayor of Hangzhou, to request protection. Zhao replied that the government could be responsible for protection within the scope of Hangzhou. However, most of the areas along the way to Ningbo, Shaoxing, and other places were rural areas. Before the Northeast Incident was resolved, the people in the mainland were deeply indignant and prone to misunderstandings. It would be safer to visit after the Northeast Incident was resolved. The Japanese Consul repeatedly requested that the Municipal Government specifically describe the contact situation at that time and submit it to the Provincial Government for review. The Provincial Government considered the handling appropriate and ordered the Municipal Government to forward a letter to the Japanese Consul, asking him to inform the students of the school to postpone their visit to the mainland. After receiving the order, the Municipal Government forwarded a letter to the Japanese Consul for reference.

The Legislative Yuan Passes the Organization Law of Primary and Secondary Schools

Nanjing, December 12th. The Legislative Yuan's committees paid close attention to secondary education. When discussing the organization law of primary and secondary schools on the morning of the 12th, members Zhao Naichuan, Cheng Zhongxing, Wang Boqiu, Zhang Mojun, Tao Xuan, and others spoke successively, discussing the purpose of primary and secondary education and the content of textbooks and teaching materials in great detail. Then Shao Yuanchong said that the Central Committee will have a proposal to rectify education at the Third Plenary Session, and the Legislative Yuan can put forward specific opinions for the Central Committee to adopt. Nanjing, December 12th. The Legislative Yuan passed the organization law of primary and secondary schools at the 210th meeting on the 12th as follows:

1. Middle School Organization Law

Article 1. Middle schools shall continue the basic training of primary schools in accordance with the educational purpose of the Republic of China and its implementation policy, so as to develop the physical and mental health of young people, cultivate healthy citizens, and prepare for advanced academic research and various occupations.

Article 2. Middle schools are divided into junior middle schools and senior middle schools, each with a three-year term of study. Junior middle schools and senior middle schools may be established in combination.

Article 3. Middle schools shall be established by provinces or cities directly under the Executive Yuan. However, in accordance with local conditions, if there is a need to establish middle schools and the facilities for primary school education are not hindered, county cities may establish them. Private individuals or groups may also establish middle schools.

Article 4. Middle schools established by provinces, cities, or counties are provincial, municipal, or county middle schools. Those jointly established by two or more counties are joint middle schools of certain counties. Those established by private individuals or groups are private middle schools.

Article 5. The establishment, change, and closure of middle schools established by provinces or cities directly under the Executive Yuan shall be filed with the Ministry of Education by the provincial and municipal education administrative organs. The rest shall be approved by the provincial and municipal education administrative organs and forwarded to the Ministry of Education for filing.

Article 6. The teaching subjects and curriculum standards of middle schools shall be determined by the Ministry of Education. Middle schools shall set up vocational subjects separately according to local needs.

Article 7. Middle school textbooks shall adopt those compiled or approved by the Ministry of Education.

Article 8. Middle schools shall have one principal who shall be responsible for the overall school affairs. For provincial middle schools, the Education Department shall submit qualified personnel, who shall be employed after being approved by the Provincial Government Committee. For municipal middle schools in cities directly under the Executive Yuan, the municipal education administrative organ shall recommend qualified personnel and submit them to the municipal government for approval. For county municipal middle schools, the county municipal government shall recommend qualified personnel and submit them to the Education Department for approval. In addition to teaching courses in the school, they shall not hold other positions concurrently. The employment of the aforementioned middle school principals shall be submitted to the Ministry of Education for filing by the provincial and municipal education administrative organs on a regular basis. The principal of a private middle school shall be selected by the school's attack team and hired, and shall be submitted to the competent education administrative organ for filing.

Article 9. Middle school teachers shall be hired by the principal and shall be full-time. However, in special circumstances, part-time teachers may be hired, and the number of them shall not exceed one-fourth of the total number of teachers. Middle school staff shall be appointed by the principal and shall be submitted to the competent education administrative organ for filing.

Article 10. The regulations for the employment of middle school principals and teachers shall be determined by the Ministry of Education.

Article 11. The admission qualification for senior middle school shall be graduation from a public or registered private junior middle school. In areas where the number of junior middle school graduates is too small, students with equivalent academic ability may be recruited, but they shall not exceed one-fifth of the total number of students admitted. The admission qualification for junior middle school shall be graduation from a public or registered private primary school or having equivalent academic ability. All students shall pass the entrance examination.

Article 12. Students who have completed the course of study at a junior or senior middle school and have passed the examination shall be given a graduation certificate by the school.

Article 13. The middle school regulations shall be determined by the Ministry of Education.

Article 14. This law shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

2. Primary School Organization Law

Article 1. Primary schools shall follow the educational purpose and implementation policy of the Republic of China to develop children's physical and mental health, cultivate the moral foundation of citizens, and the basic knowledge and skills necessary for life.

Article 2. The term of study for primary school is six years. The first four years are the junior primary school, and the last two years are the senior primary school. Junior primary schools may be established separately according to local conditions.

Article 3. Primary schools shall be established by cities, counties, townships, towns, districts, and neighborhoods. In special circumstances, they may be established by provinces. Private individuals or groups may also establish primary schools.

Article 4. Primary schools established by cities or counties are municipal or county primary schools. Those established by districts are district primary schools. Those established by townships, towns, or neighborhoods are township, town, or neighborhood primary schools. Those jointly established by two or more districts, two or more townships, towns, or two or more neighborhoods are certain district, certain township, town, or certain neighborhood primary schools. Those established by private individuals or groups are private primary schools.

Article 5. The primary school attached to the normal school is the primary school attached to the normal school.

Article 6. The change and closure of primary schools within the provincial administrative region, except for those established by the province, shall be approved by the competent county and city education administrative organs and submitted to the Education Department for filing. In the area of a city directly under the Executive Yuan, it shall be approved by the municipal education administrative organ.

Article 7. Primary school classes shall use a single-class system. However, in special circumstances, a complex-class system may be used. In junior primary schools, a two-part or single-class system may be used.

Article 8. The teaching subjects and curriculum standards of primary schools shall be determined by the Ministry of Education. Senior primary schools shall set up simple vocational subjects according to local conditions.

Article 9. Primary school textbooks shall adopt those compiled or approved by the Ministry of Education. The compilation or approval of the aforementioned items shall also pay attention to local teaching materials.

Article 10. Primary schools may be attached to kindergartens.

Article 11. Primary schools shall have one principal who shall be responsible for the overall school affairs. The principals of provincial or municipal primary schools directly under the Executive Yuan shall be selected and employed by the Education Department or the municipal education administrative organ. The principals of county, municipal, district, neighborhood, or township primary schools shall be selected by the county and city education administrative organs and submitted to the county and city governments for employment, and submitted to the Education Department for filing. The principals of private primary schools shall be employed by the school board of directors or the founder after a qualified person. And submit to the competent education administrative organ for filing. The principal of the affiliated primary school shall be appointed by the principal of the competent school and shall be submitted to the competent education administrative organ for filing. However, if the affiliated primary school of a private school has special circumstances and a separate school board of directors is established, it shall be employed by the school board of directors.

Article 12. Primary school teachers shall be hired by the principal after a qualified person. If there is a shortage of qualified persons, those with equivalent qualifications may be hired. All shall be submitted to the competent education administrative organ for filing. The regulations for the assessment, employment, and protection of primary school teachers shall be determined by the Ministry of Education.

Article 13. Primary school principals and teachers shall be full-time principals, and they shall also teach courses in the school.

Article 14. Primary schools may be set up separately or jointly to set up school police or nursing staff. Those with six or more classes may set up clerks as appropriate.

Article 15. Students who have completed the course of study in junior or senior primary school and have passed the examination shall be given a graduation certificate by the school.

Article 16. Primary schools do not charge tuition fees. However, they may collect fees as appropriate depending on local conditions. In public primary schools, the maximum fee for each person per semester shall not exceed one yuan for junior primary school and two yuan for senior primary school. If private primary schools charge tuition fees, the maximum fee for each person per semester shall not exceed three yuan for junior primary school and eight yuan for senior primary school. If students are unable to pay tuition fees, the primary school principal shall consider the circumstances and waive part or all of their tuition fees.

Article 17. The primary school regulations shall be determined by the Ministry of Education.

Article 18. This law shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

The Reorganization of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the Arrival of Orders in Shanghai

The General Manager's Office Completes Preparations

The New General Manager to Take Office Tomorrow

Consideration of Stock Value Requested by Li

Explanation of Wharf Loan Procedures

Since the reorganization of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (CMSNC) was discussed and decided upon separately by the Central Political Council and the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Communications yesterday issued an order to the Supervisory Office, instructing it to order General Manager Li Guojie to hand over his duties. It also ordered General Manager Liu Hongsheng to take office immediately, and notified the directors and supervisors to perform their duties. General Manager Li has completed the handover, and the new General Manager is scheduled to take office tomorrow. Regarding the wharf loan mortgage case, the staff firmly opposed it, and General Manager Li specially published the details of the process. The details are recorded as follows:

The Ministry of Communications' Order Arrives in Shanghai: New General Manager Liu Hongsheng, Standing Director Ye Zhuotang, Director Hu Bijang, and Supervisor Lu Xuepu, etc., formally received the appointment order from the Ministry of Communications yesterday. Supervisor Chen Fumu also received instructions from the Ministry of Communications yesterday to hand over his duties one by one. He then forwarded the order to General Manager Li Guojie to comply with. The original order is recorded as follows: Order to Comply with Instructions. It is hereby ordered that the reorganization of the China Merchants Bureau has been discussed and decided separately by the Central Political Conference and the Executive Yuan, and the Executive Yuan has presented a request to the National Government to appoint Ye Zhuotang, etc., as Standing Directors, Hu Bijang, etc., as Directors, Lu Xuepu, etc., as Supervisors, and Liu Hongsheng as General Manager. The Ministry hereby orders the said General Manager Liu Hongsheng to proceed to the Bureau to take office immediately and notify the Directors and Supervisors to convene a meeting to perform their duties. In addition to informing the said Manager, the Ministry also forwards the information to the former General Manager of the Bureau, Li Guojie, to acknowledge and handle accordingly, and to report separately. It is appropriate to order you to comply with this order and hand over your duties one by one. We hereby order the said General Manager to immediately comply with this order and hand over your duties.

▲ Completion of Handling in Compliance with Orders. After Supervisor Chen Fumu of the Supervisory Office submitted his resignation, he was immediately ordered to complete the handover and prepare to hand over his duties. All kinds of documents have been compiled with numbers and completed. General Manager Li Guojie of the General Manager's Office, after the Executive Yuan's meeting resolved to reorganize, immediately instructed the heads of the Secretariat and the General Affairs, Business, Shipping, Wharf Affairs, Accounting, and Commercial departments to be responsible for handling the handover separately in order to prepare for the transfer. The various departments have been rushing to complete this work for several days, and it is expected to be completed within a few days. In the future, the functions and powers of the Supervisory Office will be replaced by the Board of Supervisors in accordance with the resolution of the Executive Yuan, and the Supervisory Office will naturally be abolished.

▲ Liu Dingming to Take Office. New General Manager Liu Hongsheng received instructions from the Ministry of Communications yesterday morning, ordering him to go to the China Merchants Bureau to take office immediately. Today is Sunday. According to sources from the Bureau yesterday, Liu Dingming will come to the Bureau to take office on the 14th.

▲ Minister Zhu's Attitude. After the Central Government decided to nationalize the China Merchants Bureau, the Bureau's General Manager Li Guojie secretly mortgaged the Bureau's four wharves to the American-owned China General Edison Company for debt, and signed a contract to implement the takeover the day before yesterday. The Ministry of Communications received a telegram that day and immediately dispatched Gao Tingzi, Director of the Navigation Administration Department, to fly to Shanghai to investigate the truth. He returned to Beijing by night train that evening to report to Minister Zhu and request instructions on how to deal with the matter. Zhu Jiahua stated, "This matter is of utmost importance to national sovereignty. The Ministry had no prior knowledge of Li Guojie's mortgaging of the Bureau's assets to foreign merchants for a huge amount of money. It was only after the contract was signed the day before yesterday that we received a telegram from General Manager Liu Hongsheng. We immediately dispatched Gao Tingzi, Director of the Navigation Administration Department, to fly to Shanghai to investigate. He brought back the contract for the mortgage signed by both parties to Beijing this morning (the 12th). It is currently under thorough study. The amount of the loan reached more than 20 million. General Manager Li's reasons are nothing more than to repay various urgent debts and to circulate funds. However, since the Central Government has resolved to nationalize the China Merchants Bureau, it should await instructions. It is suspected of exceeding his authority to sign a loan to foreigners without authorization. How to deal with this in the future will be discussed after reviewing the contract. In short, national sovereignty will not be allowed to be abandoned in the slightest." Gao Tingzi also stated, "I was ordered by the Ministry to fly to Shanghai to investigate the loan matter of the China Merchants Bureau. After arriving in Shanghai, I met General Manager Li Guojie and obtained the signed contract and a large number of other documents related to this case. Although Li made some explanations for handling this matter, it is inevitable that people will find it puzzling that he did not report to the Ministry for instructions beforehand. While in Shanghai, I also consulted the new General Manager Liu Hongsheng and the directors about their opinions on this case and remedial and follow-up measures. This morning, I personally presented the original text of the contract to Minister Zhu and requested instructions on how to deal with it. Due to foreign relations, it cannot be published. However, the Ministry of Communications will handle it impartially due to the issue of jurisdiction. There will be a strict disposition of this case." It is also heard that Minister of Communications Zhu Jiahua telegraphed Han yesterday to report to Jiang and Song and request instructions on how to deal with the matter. A reply has not yet been received. Also, Li only sent Secretary Yang with the contract he signed and a written explanation to the Ministry on the evening of the 11th. It is said that the original case is very long. The Ministry of Communications is currently studying the content of the contract. Since this matter has been formally signed, there is a legal basis. Although we intend to cancel it, we are afraid that the foreign merchants will not agree. After research, it is planned to negotiate with the company. The Ministry of Communications will handle this case on the principle of not losing sovereignty. It is also heard that Zhu Jiahua plans to go to Shanghai on the evening of the 13th to personally investigate the truth and meet with the new General Manager of the China Merchants Bureau, Liu Hongsheng, to discuss everything.

▲ Li Guojie's Telegram to the Ministry. Li Guojie, Chairman and General Manager of the China Merchants Bureau, telegraphed to Song, President of the Executive Yuan in Nanjing, and Zhu, Minister of Communications, "Respectfully to the attention of Song, President of the Executive Yuan, and Zhu, Minister of Communications: Reports state that the China Merchants Bureau was resolved by the Central Political Council on the 9th to be nationalized, and all stocks will be returned to shareholders at the market price of 50 taels per set. While the government is indeed showing consideration for the difficulties of merchants, the shareholders still suffer significant losses. An investigation reveals that the total assets of the China Merchants Bureau and its accumulated property company are estimated to be worth 50 to 60 million taels at current prices. After deducting more than 17 million to repay debts, there remains 30 to 40 million. If the company were to be dissolved and liquidated, each set of shares would be worth more than 1,000 taels. Now, only 5% of the value is being used to nationalize the shipping assets and the real estate unrelated to the shipping industry that has been analyzed and reorganized into a separate company. Not only are the shareholders unable to legally enjoy the profits that have been generated and grown over the past 60 years, but even the initial investment of capital is being lost by more than half. This does not seem to be the intention of our wise government to treat merchants with fairness and generosity. Based on the regulations on supervising privately-owned public utility enterprises promulgated by the government and passed by the Legislative Yuan, the nationalization, the counting of the amount of assets of private enterprises, and the evaluation and recovery of assets are all clearly stated in the laws, which are visible to all at home and abroad and are jointly respected. How can we only use the current low price of buying and selling stocks by one or two shareholders as the standard? Moreover, the rise and fall of stock prices are uncertain, while the amount of asset value is fixed. If we abandon the fundamentals and only pursue the superficial, it will inevitably make domestic industrialists hesitate. Especially for the accumulated property company unrelated to the shipping industry, it should be handled separately. Because I have been heavily entrusted by the shareholders and the matter concerns the interests of the entire body, I dare not remain silent. I humbly request that you adopt this suggestion, reconsider it, and I am extremely grateful and moved. Furthermore, I have heard that a capable person has been selected for the position of General Manager. Please instruct him to come to the Bureau as soon as possible to take over, so that I can be relieved of my heavy burden. I respectfully submit this combined telegram. Li Guojie, Chairman and General Manager of the China Merchants Bureau."

▲ Explanation of Wharf Loan. The loans recommended by Li Guojie to the Supervisory Office before taking office included three types: one was a construction loan, the second was a wharf loan, and the third was a purchase of new ships on credit. The one that has been implemented by signing a contract is the wharf loan. The explanation of the wharf loan is recorded as follows: The wharf loan is to re-borrow and mortgage the wharves of the five new wharves of Central, Northern, China and Southern China owned by the China Merchants Bureau, which had already been mortgaged to the Hongkong and Shanghai Banking Corporation, to the American-owned China General Edison Company. The company will issue bonds with a total face value of 10 million Shanghai taels, which will be used to repay the old HSBC debt and redeem the mortgaged properties in various ports at home and abroad, in order to create a new plan for activities. The points that need to be explained for this loan are: ㈠ The urgency of the HSBC debt and the concern of bankruptcy. The largest creditor of the China Merchants Bureau is the Hongkong and Shanghai Banking Corporation, with a debt of 5 million taels of principal, plus interest, donations and taxes paid on its behalf over the years, totaling approximately 2 million taels, for a total of more than 7 million taels. The mortgages are the five wharf of Central, North, China, South (i.e. Jin Liyuan) and New (i.e. Yangjiadu) in this port, and the real estate in Hankou, Tianjin, Wenzhou, Ningbo, Shantou, Qianjiang Wuhu, Jiujiang, Shashi, Yichang and other foreign ports. According to the valuation made by Tongli Foreign Firm four years ago, the above-mentioned mortgages are worth about 20 million taels of silver. However, a loan of less than a quarter of the value has caused such valuable property to be completely mortgaged and unable to be used, which is a pity. In recent years, the bank has expressed dissatisfaction with the excessive arrears of interest. According to the original contract, the bank demanded repayment of principal and interest, and the momentum was strong. Last year, former Commissioner Guo also promised to repay it at the end of the year, but was unable to do so. Therefore, the urging was even more urgent. Although the Board of Directors has made every effort to respond, it has fortunately not broken down. However, how can it be possible to get away with empty words for a long time? If we do not take this opportunity to quickly raise a huge sum of money to repay the bank and redeem all the mortgaged properties to get rid of this disaster and find another way out, in case of a breakdown, and the bank disposes of the mortgaged properties everywhere, other creditors will inevitably follow suit. Then, in the midst of the Chu song on all sides, it will be impossible for the China Merchants Bureau to avoid bankruptcy. ㈡ The only main reason for the sluggish business. The reason why the debts of the China Merchants Bureau have become increasingly heavy is purely due to the sluggish business. The only tools that the business relies on are ships and warehouses and wharves. However, the Bureau only has 25 ships left, and most of them are too old to be used. The warehouses and wharves are also old and dilapidated, and have lost their production capacity, resulting in more expenditure and less income. The shortfall is all made up by borrowing money, so it loses money every year and incurs more debt every year. The debt platform is getting higher and higher, and the life is becoming increasingly difficult. Therefore, if we do not urgently seek to add ships and actively repair the warehouses and wharves to revitalize the business and increase revenue, then those who rely on borrowing money to live will inevitably die from the suffering of the debt burden. This can be said with certainty. ㈢ The negotiation and conditions of the loan. The negotiation of this loan began in the winter of last year, after Guojie and former Commissioner Guo agreed on the overall plan. Then, in connection with the aforementioned construction loan, negotiations were started with the American-owned China General Edison Company. After the company fully accepted it, it went on to discuss the conditions. The China General Edison Company will provide the Bureau with a loan of up to 10 million Shanghai taels, with the wharves and real estate of the five Central, Northern, China and Southern wharves under the jurisdiction of the China Merchants Bureau as collateral. The term is 20 years and the interest rate is 9% per annum. However, because this kind of huge loan is beyond the company's ability to bear, it is allowed to issue bonds worth 10 million taels in its own name or in the name of the designated person. In order to encourage bondholders to sell easily in view of the current tight world financial situation, it was agreed by both parties that the actual amount of this loan must be received at a discount of 85%. The company is responsible for whether the bonds can be sold and how to pay interest and repay principal, which has nothing to do with the Bureau. In addition, the interest of 9% is initially considered to be slightly heavy, but since the Shanghai War, the money market has not eased. According to the past lending practices, the HSBC debt interest rate was already 8% ten years ago, and the Citibank interest rate was even 8.5%. Moreover, before the wharves and warehouses are completed, the income is limited, and the interest is not enough for the company to pay for us every year. Therefore, the number of 9% is still not considered to be a heavy interest under the current market situation. Even the 2.5% commission it demanded is also a customary practice in fact and cannot be admitted without pain. The above-mentioned loan is used to repay all the HSBC mortgages, the interest payable, and the various donations and taxes paid on its behalf, totaling approximately 7 million taels. In addition, the old debts that should be cleared for the wharf, such as the debts owed to the Siming Bank and Sandetang, totaled approximately 100,000 taels. In addition, 250,000 taels will be paid to the commission that should be paid for this loan. The first half of the plan for this loan is to repay the debt, redeem the mortgaged properties, and its conditions are as follows. ㈣ The lease and transfer of the wharf. In the above-mentioned conditions, the China Merchants Bureau, except for reserving the Southern Wharf (i.e. Jin Liyuan Wharf) for its own use and the New Wharf (i.e. Yangjiadu Wharf) for its own operation, the China General Edison Company will lease all of the Central, Northern and China three wharves from the date of signing this loan. The annual rent is stipulated to be a total of 300,000 Shanghai taels for a period of 20 years. After the expiration date, the lessee is willing to continue to continue for another 10 years. The Central, Northern and China three wharves are used to promote foreign shipping and have nothing to do with domestic shipping. In peacetime, they only solicit foreign ship business. Over the years, the annual income is only more than 200,000 taels in addition to expenses. If the rent that should be obtained by leasing to others is measured, not only is there no pure profit to be said, but also tens of thousands of taels are still collected less every year. Now, the Central, Northern and China three wharves have a guaranteed rent of 300,000 taels per year without any effort on our part. All the donations and taxes currently and in the future levied on the leased wharf by the Shanghai Municipal Council or the Chinese government are the responsibility of the lessee to pay. The amount saved every year is not small, and the New Wharf is still reserved for its own operation. The total income is higher than before, and it can be guaranteed. It is also agreed that the lessee may sub-lease or transfer it to a third party at the same rent, but the term shall not exceed the final due date stipulated in these conditions. This third party is the Dalae Shipping Company, which was previously jointly accepted by the Bureau for this loan. Because the Bureau's previous lease term was too long, although the rent was not short, it was still not very cost-effective when the property price and interest were compared. Therefore, it was agreed with the Dalae Company to jointly establish a Central, Northern and China three wharves company with the Bureau to operate the ship mooring and cargo piling business, and to regain half of the business rights of the wharf, etc. The second half of the plan for this mortgage to protect property and develop business and its conditions are as follows. ㈤ The right to jointly establish a wharf company. After the China General Edison Company agrees to transfer the three leased wharves to the Dalae Shipping Company, it will be used to jointly establish a wharf company with the Bureau. Both parties will each invest 1 million taels of capital. The company is also willing to raise debts and provide advances for this capital required by our side. All the conditions shall be in accordance with the bond method of this loan. It is difficult for the Bureau to raise this huge capital separately, and it has regained half of the business rights of the three wharves. The Dalae Shipping Company is very large in scale and has dozens of ocean-going vessels that regularly travel to Europe, America, Japan, and Southeast Asia. The Bureau's original business customers, coupled with the ocean-going vessels that regularly berth at Dalae, are the basis. The interest on wharf rentals and cargo handling will naturally not be less, and Dalae can also solicit other Southeast Asian shipping business. The surplus profit is divided equally in half. Compared with completely self-operation, the degree of development cannot be counted by kilometers. Moreover, there is a guaranteed rent of 300,000 yuan per year. Although the term is longer, the profit is also larger. In any case, the Bureau will definitely not suffer a loss. ㈥ Preparation for paying principal and interest. In order to prepare to pay the interest on this mortgage and to plan to have funds every year in order to pay the money into the debt repayment reserve account, the following income is designated for its use: ㈠ The annual rent of the Central, Northern and China three wharves, ㈡ The wharf rentals that the Southern and New wharves should pay on schedule. ㈢ 25% of the net profit from the shipping business in the future. The above income will first be used to pay the interest on this mortgage. If there is a surplus in the total amount of income, it will be included in the reserve account for the China Merchants Bureau to repay the debt for future payment of the principal. This accumulated reserve fund will be managed by the China General Edison Company and must be devised to generate the maximum possible interest. However, if the China Merchants Bureau has a good strategy that can make the interest generate generous returns, it is suggested that the company adopt it. This generated interest will also be included in the debt repayment reserve account and shall not be used for other purposes. ㈦ All related benefits. In summary, the main purpose of this loan is to raise a sum of money to repay the Hongkong and Shanghai Banking Corporation in order to avoid the danger of bankruptcy. The related benefits are: ㈠ To repay the old debts of the Siming Bank and Sandetang, ㈡ To redeem the real estate in various ports, which can be used as collateral for the purchase of new ships on credit, ㈢ The Central, Northern and China three wharves can be leased at the same time, with a guaranteed annual rent income, ㈣ The Southern and New wharves can still be used and operated by ourselves without any restrictions, ㈤ To borrow other people's capital to build and add various houses on the Central, Northern and China three wharves and the rest of the wharf land, ㈥ To jointly establish a wharf company, develop the business, and receive half of its rights, and to borrow other people's capital to raise this capital for us. It is a good opportunity to prepare for several good things at once. Therefore, Guojie believes that this kind of good opportunity should not be missed, lest the China Merchants Bureau fall into a state of poverty and sit and wait to die.

▲ Chen Supervisor's Report. Regarding this loan plan, Li Guojie reported to Chen Fumu, Supervisor of the Bureau, last month. We can understand its content by reading it. The original report stated, "For the matter of reporting, I, Guojie, previously submitted a report on the reorganization of the China Merchants Bureau's loan situation, attaching copies of the construction loan contract with the Shanghai Bund Fuzhou Road area, the mortgage contract, the Shanghai Central, Northern, China, New and Southern five wharves loan contract, the mortgage contract, the Shanghai Central, Northern and China three wharves lease contract, and the memorandum on purchasing ships on credit, requesting your approval. I received instructions stating, "The report and various mortgage contracts, loan contracts, leases and explanatory documents have been received. An investigation reveals that the China Merchants Bureau's debts are accumulating, and the ships and warehouses are dilapidated, resulting in a decline in business and a monthly deficit of more than 100,000. If we do not plan to thoroughly improve it as soon as possible, it will become bankrupt. According to the report, the agreements with the American-owned China General Edison Company and the Dalae Shipping Company, such as the construction loan in the Shanghai Bund Fuzhou Road area, the Shanghai Central, Northern, China, New and Southern five wharves mortgage loan, the Shanghai Central, Northern and China three wharves lease contract, and the memorandum on purchasing ships on credit, have been repeatedly discussed by former Commissioner Guo Waifeng and the General Manager. Now, the various contracts and articles have been reviewed by this office and are still feasible. In accordance with the provisions of the regulations, they should be approved for record. The General Manager should separately sign the above-mentioned contracts with the American merchants, etc. In addition to using the borrowed funds to repay the accumulated debts, the remainder should be designated for construction and production, so as to enable the stagnant situation to be revived and avoid wasting the funds and increasing the debts. You should comply with this order." I, Guojie, complied and contacted the American-owned China General Edison Company, and formally signed the above-mentioned construction loan contract, the mortgage contract, the wharf lease contract, and the memorandum on purchasing ships on credit on September 5th and 6th this year. However, the Yi Company stated that the signing of the above-mentioned contracts was approved by the Supervisor, and the Supervisor should affix the official seal to complete the legal procedures. I hereby attach the original and duplicate copies of the various contracts, mortgage contracts, and memorandums that have been signed, and request your approval to affix the official seal and return them for separate possession. Furthermore, according to the China General Edison Company, the issuance of bonds for the above-mentioned loans still requires a considerable period of preparation. Before the arrangement is in place, both parties should temporarily keep it secret, etc. I hereby report this combined information and request your examination. Respectfully presented by Chen, Vice Minister of Communications and Supervisor of the China Merchants Bureau, and Li Guojie, General Manager of the China Merchants Bureau. (Huadong News Agency)"

▲ Secretary-General Zeng's Talk. Yesterday, a reporter visited the Secretariat of the Bureau's Supervisory Office, and according to Hui Huaiwen, the loan reorganization of the China Merchants Bureau was planned by Guo Waifeng when he was in office. The loan from the American-owned China General Edison Company was 10 million taels for a construction loan and 10 million taels for a wharf loan. In addition, because the American-owned China General Edison Company and the Dalae Shipping Company are related, Dalae will purchase new ships from abroad on credit. It is planned to purchase 30 ships, each with a deadweight of 10,000 tons. This will also cost about 10 million taels. The loan will be used as the China Merchants Bureau's debt. The mortgages are the existing ships and wharves in this port and other ports. It is estimated that it can be repaid in 20 years. As for ㈠ the 10 million taels for the construction loan, the China General Edison Company will not deliver actual funds. The company will issue public bonds to renovate the buildings of the China Merchants Bureau. Because the Bureau's real estate currently only earns 200,000 yuan per year, if a 13-story building is renovated, at least 1 million yuan of rent can be earned per year. ㈡ The wharf loan will be used to reorganize the wharf, and all the old and scattered mortgages will be redeemed at the same time. After the China General Edison Company takes over, it will only have the right to supervise, manage, design and reform. If the business develops and various payments are received every day, the company will be responsible for the safekeeping. Because Dalae has a loan relationship, all Dalae's incoming and outgoing vessels will rely on the wharves of the China Merchants Bureau, and an annual rent of 300,000 taels will be subsidized. In the future, a wharf company will be established to be solely responsible. ㈢ The purchase of new ships on credit is because the China Merchants Bureau's vessels are old and were purchased 30 or 40 years ago. Not only is the tonnage small, but it is also very dangerous to sail at sea. This method is indeed needed now. The wharf dispute was indeed unclear beforehand. Therefore, after the representative came to the Bureau, it was resolved. However, the shareholders believe that the previous face value of the shares was 100 taels, but the Ministry of Communications ordered the shares to be repurchased at 50 taels, which they feel is too much of a loss and there is a slight problem. The Supervisory Office will be abolished after the establishment of the Board of Supervisors, etc. (Guowen News Agency)

A Glimpse of the Contract Content. Although the loan contract signed between the China Merchants Bureau and the China General Edison Company is for 30 million taels, the preliminary agreement for building houses for 1,000 taels was signed in September this year. The official contract was signed by Li after he took office and Sadeley, the General Manager of the China General Edison Company. The loan will be distributed to the China Merchants Bureau by issuing public bonds at 85% of the actual amount. The China General Edison Company is responsible for everything. 4 million taels will be issued first for the following purposes: A. To repay the 1 million taels loan and interest that was previously mortgaged at Citibank. B. To repay the 470,000 taels loan and interest that was previously mortgaged at the China General Edison Company. C. To pay the Bureau 500,000 taels to meet the needs of business. D. To pay the construction costs of building the newest office building at the corner of Sichuan Road and Fuzhou Road. E. To pay the China General Edison Company the 2.5% commission that should be obtained according to the face value of the first batch of bonds issued for the mortgage loan. (Guowen News Agency)

▲ Observation of the Four Wharf Manager's Office. After Ling Jingshan submitted his resignation to General Manager Li of the General Management Office of the China Merchants Bureau on the afternoon of the day before yesterday, he handed over his affairs to Deputy Section Chief Hong Dezhao as an agent. Li Guojie approved Ling's leave for 15 days because Ling refused to hand over his affairs to the China General Edison Company but had handed over his affairs, and appointed Hong Dezhao to succeed Ling. At the same time, the China General Edison Company sent Zhong Ketuo to the Four Wharf Manager's Office to jointly take charge. Yesterday was the birthday of General Sun Yat-sen. The office was ordered by the General Management Office to close for one day and still hung the national flag to commemorate the event.

Page 14

▲ Wharf Workers Petition. The Five Wharf Workers' Union decided on three measures at a joint meeting of all group leaders regarding the wharf mortgage matter. Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 p.m., a council meeting was held, presided over by Yu Xianting, who reported on the process. Then, the discussion began, and the resolutions of the joint meeting of group leaders were unanimously passed. It was decided that tomorrow at 10:00 a.m., all matters would be handled by Yu Xianting, Xue Yinkui, Shi Tiezhang, Zhang Guiqing, Cheng Changsheng, etc., together with all group leaders Xia Zhende, Wang Xingcun, Lin Sheng, Xue Xingbiao, Zhao Zule, etc., to petition the General Bureau. ㈠ Oppose the mortgage as the highest principle and protect livelihood as the minimum. ㈡ Expedite the case of the salary arrears in October. (Xinsheng News Agency)

▲ General Bureau Workers Oppose. Regarding the wharf mortgage, the General Bureau Workers' Union, in addition to sending a letter to the General Manager stating its firm opposition, also sent a telegram stating, "Respectfully to the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Communications, all levels of Party Headquarters, all organs, all organizations, and all newspaper offices: Recently, a Westerner suddenly came to take over the Central, Northern, and China three wharves of this Bureau. We learned that the three wharves' properties and business management have been transferred to foreign merchants. The colleagues are extremely shocked. The China Merchants Bureau is the only remaining transportation enterprise in our country. Now that the government has determined to actually take it over and run it as a national enterprise, we are looking forward to proper rectification and daily prosperity. The Central, Northern, and China three wharves are the only business tool of this Bureau. The several wharves in Shanghai have long been coveted by foreign merchants. The Chinese people are unable to wait to protect and support them, how can we bear to abandon them like worn-out shoes and hand them over? In this reorganization of a storm-tossed and precarious situation, there is suddenly a move to transfer the three wharves to foreign merchants. Such a blatant sacrifice of shipping tools is a loss of sovereignty and humiliation. The colleagues and the China Merchants Bureau share weal and woe and are closely related. What we feel is dangerous, and we cannot remain silent. We vow not to recognize this illegal act. In addition to stating our firm opposition to the Supervisor and General Manager of this Bureau, we also hope that all compatriots in the country will unite to support us in saving the nation's shipping industry, we are most fortunate. Respectfully, the Shanghai China Merchants Steam Navigation General Bureau Workers' Union. (Xinsheng News Agency)"

The Second Day of the Chinese Children's Education Society Annual Meeting

丨Discussing Health Education and Elementary School Textbook Issues丨

Holding a Ceremony to Celebrate the Birthday of the Premier

The third annual meeting of the Chinese Children's Education Society continued at Nanzhong Elementary School on the morning of the 12th at about 9 o'clock. Because that day was the Premier's birthday, Chairman Ma Ketan and Master of Ceremonies Tian Shuren held a ceremony to celebrate the Premier's birthday. Ma Ketan then spoke about the greatness of the Premier's life and career, followed by an introduction of Dr. Jiang Benkuan, who lectured on the state of mental health in the United States.

▲ Details of Proposal Discussions

Ma Ketan then reported on the formal discussion of the proposals. Cha Shouhong and He Erchao took records. First, they reported that some organizations were planning to join the society through introductions. However, individual members only needed approval from two executive committees, while group members required approval from the general assembly. The names of the schools were then put forward, including the Veterans' School, Jiangsu Provincial Women's Normal School, Fujian Jimei Experimental Rural Normal School, and Fujian Provincial Fuzhou Elementary School, all of which were approved one by one. The report then stated that the proposals had been sorted into five categories: ㈠ Health Education, ㈡ Curriculum, Teaching Materials, and Textbook Research, ㈢ Children's Publications, ㈣ Society Affairs, ㈤ Other. The first category was then discussed: ㈠ Proposal to formulate specific standards for health performance evaluation. (The method: ㈠ Health knowledge and skills 40%, ㈡ Health habits 40%, ㈢ Physical fitness 5%, ㈣ Diseases 5%, ㈤ Overall evaluation of other academic performance 5%, ㈥ Practical ability 5%.) Chen Jianheng said that in addition to health, sociology should also be included. Some advocated that, in addition to this, attention should also be paid to sports, hygiene, safety, etc. Some said that special attention should be paid to health habits and that schools should be designated for experimentation. Some said that there are many issues related to health education and that a permanent health education committee should be organized to focus on research. It was then resolved to organize a health education committee to review and research the proposal. As for the organizational methods, given the situation of the executive committee, they would be planned and organized by the executive committee. Opinions expressed during the daytime session would be submitted to the established committee for reference. ㈡ Proposal on what method should be adopted for editing health teaching materials for senior elementary schools (the proposer reported examples: ㈠ Central question, ㈡ Small questions, ㈢ Summary, ㈣ Homework, ㈤ Habit formation, ㈥ Formal testing, ㈦ Diagnostic testing.) Some advocated submitting it to a committee for research, while others advocated free experimentation by each school. It was resolved to submit it to the Health Education Committee for research. ㈢ Proposal on standardizing children's education. Xue Tianhan and others proposed that the society should urgently standardize the normal weight standards for children that are more applicable nationwide or in various provinces and regions and that the proposals should be discussed together. With the consent of the public, it was jointly resolved to submit them to the Health Education Committee for review and research. ㈣ Proposal to compile the materials displayed at the Health Education Achievement Exhibition into an annual report. Li Qingsong and Chen Heqin advocated entrusting the Beijing Municipal Annual Report Team to handle it, which was resolved by entrusting it to the Annual Report Team. Xia Chengfeng said that this year's products are so beautiful that it may be difficult to select them in the future. Xue Tianhan said that the established selection objectives should be divided into several categories, and the best should be selected from the same achievements. Shi Renfu, Li Qingsong, and Luo Tingguang, etc., all expressed opinions on how the exhibition should be jointly organized as a reference. The second category is curriculum, teaching material, and textbook research: ㈠ Current elementary school textbook proposal (the method: the first step is for the society to investigate the elementary school textbooks adopted by group members this year and the subjects they voluntarily experiment with and research; the second step is for the society to formulate experimental record forms and distribute them to group members and allocate experimental textbooks; the third step is for the results of experimental research to be submitted to the society two months before the next general meeting; the fourth step is for the society to collect a majority of opinions and submit them to the next annual meeting for discussion and sorting; the fifth step is to publish the discussions and sorting in the monthly magazine (and suggest them to the Ministry of Education for reference in compiling textbooks). Wu Yan and Chen Heqin advocated a textbook research committee. Jiang Xicen advocated making corrections to textbooks as teaching materials, because textbooks have a small scope and teaching materials have a larger scope. Xue Tianhan seconded the motion. It was then resolved to organize an elementary school teaching material research committee. Li Qingsong proposed that the executive committee hire an organization, and everyone agreed without objection. It was past noon, and due to a visit to the mausoleum at 1 pm, it was decided to continue the meeting at 9 am on the 13th.

▲ Afternoon Visits and Socializing

At 2 o'clock, they visited the National Public Gymnasium and the Veterans' School. At 7 o'clock, a social gathering was held. In addition to the members of the society from yesterday, Wang Zuxiang, Zhu Shaoping, Yu Yansheng, Li Qingwei, Wang Hongsheng, Zhang Zhizhong, Zhu Bingheng, Wei Jingchuan, Chen Chunbao, Qian Huaigang, Cheng Zongchao, Zhao Musen, Dong Mushu, Chen Mingheng, Shi Ze, Sun Jue, Jiang Chaoying, Sun Tingzhen, Yang Zhenya, Lin Jiesheng, etc. also attended.

The resolutions passed yesterday were: ㈠ High school biology should still be designated as a required course, with Zoology 1 and Botany as electives, but Natural History should be designated as a required course for normal schools. ㈡ An applied chemistry course should be added to the high school elective courses. ㈢ A course on mineralogy and geology should be added to junior high school. ㈣ The Chinese version should be the principle for science textbooks. ㈤ Each school should collect local natural products and man-made objects that can be used as teaching materials so that schools can exchange them with each other to make teaching more practical. Nantong Middle School is responsible for drafting the plan and submitting it to the Chairman of the Provincial Education Association to send a circular to all schools. In the afternoon, they visited the Tianchu MSG Factory, Tianyuan Electrochemistry Factory, and the Academia Sinica. The meeting continued at 9 am today.

The Municipal Education Bureau Pays Attention to Extracurricular Activities of Primary and Secondary School Students

Establishing Items and Distributing Them to Various Schools

The Municipal Education Bureau issued an order to primary and secondary schools in this city yesterday, stating that extracurricular activities for students in various schools are very important. The central plan for this year is health education, so extracurricular activities should also focus on health education. In addition, national crisis and labor should be used as supplements. The extracurricular activity items for this semester have been established by this bureau and are copied and distributed with the order. Each school should consider its own situation and must adopt several types for implementation and report to the bureau for record. They are ordered to comply with and handle the matter accordingly. The extracurricular activity items for primary and secondary school students for this semester are as follows: ㈠ Various sports (track and field, ball games, martial arts, swimming, soft gymnastics, apparatus exercises, etc.), ㈡ Various cleaning tasks (general cleaning, fly catching, etc.), ㈢ Various lectures (hygiene, national crisis, common sense of science, etc.), ㈣ Various exhibitions (health education history, geography, achievements, etc.), ㈤ Various group activities (student government, cooperatives, and academic, literary, music, and drama groups, etc.), ㈥ Student speech contests or debates (the themes should focus on health and national crisis), ㈦ Fire prevention work, ㈧ School road and campus construction work, ㈨ Classroom service, ㈩ Dormitory service, ㈩㈠ Excursions or hikes, ㈩㈡ Collecting and making specimens,

The Shanghai Municipal Council Normal School is Full

The Acting Superintendent of Education of the Shanghai Municipal Council recently reported to the Education Committee that the Normal School has admitted 60 students, including 35 external students, who have paid a total of 520 yuan in tuition. Wusong Tongji University Expands Campus

Since Wusong was devastated by the violent Japanese, most of the school buildings were destroyed by ruthless artillery shells. Tongji University has made every effort to rectify the situation this semester and has gradually repaired all the houses to restore their former appearance. After the Medical College of National Central University was changed to Shanghai National Medical College, it was decided to move to a new site on Haig Road for operation. The remaining Wusong campus was decided to be transferred to Tongji University for the expansion of its affiliated middle school. It is heard that President Weng Zhilong and President Yan Fuqing negotiated back and forth several times to form a transfer contract. It is reported that the formal handover will take place on the 17th of this month. Tongji has now hired workers to bid for the renovation, and the construction will be completed this year. The affiliated middle school will then move in.

Jinda Chrysanthemum Exhibition - Day One

Thousands of Guests Yesterday, Continuing Today

Also Holding an Exhibition of Japanese Army Relics

Jinru Jie Li Jinan University held a chrysanthemum exhibition yesterday, starting on the Premier's birthday, for two consecutive days. The reporter drove there yesterday afternoon and saw that the three public buses running between Shanghai and Jinru were full of passengers going to visit the school. Inquiring with the school's signatory staff, it was said that there were a total of two or three thousand guests that day. Everyone regards the school as the only overseas Chinese university in China. This Shanghai incident was just the headquarters of our heroic 19th Route Army stationed to resist the violent Japanese, and then the Japanese army was stationed for four months, and the site was severely damaged. Therefore, they took this opportunity to take a look. The school gate had a white cloth banner hanging high, "Post-War Chrysanthemum Conference." The Science Museum and Zhiyuan Hall, two major buildings, stood on a vast plain of grass. It was late autumn, and the grass had turned goose yellow, and the shadows of the sun and shadows were very lovely. Following the sign, we proceeded to the Hongnian Library Chrysanthemum Exhibition. The museum was surrounded by flowers and trees, in good order, as if it were not after a robbery. Outside the museum, the roads were lined with plane trees, and there was a small stream. The wind blew the falling leaves, which was quite poetic.

The venue was guarded by boy scouts. From the entrance to the signing place, after signing, the reception staff gave each person a chrysanthemum special issue and a chrysanthemum cultivation method. There were more than a dozen pots of large chrysanthemums on the road, all of rare varieties. Then, we entered the eastern exhibition room. At first glance, it was like entering a country of fragrance. There were three major rows in total. Although the number of pots was less than that of the Municipal Agricultural Field, the room was densely packed. Among them, varieties such as Longyan, White Jade Belt, Xueqing Maoci, and Bai were valuable. The main building of the East Room displayed the school's library club works, as well as the works of Xie Gongzhan, a well-known chrysanthemum artist from China. Xie is a painting professor. In addition, there are Shen Weisou and other books collected by Long Zhengsheng, director of the Chinese Language Department of the school, as well as true manuscripts of famous artists from the Song, Yuan, and Ming dynasties. In the West Room, there are dozens of Han monument tree books recently unearthed, as well as photographs of Ming artifacts, which are not easily seen outside. On the long table in the north, there were also wooden clogs, monk's robes, blood canvas beds used by the National Rescue Team, pictures sent by Japanese elementary school students to encourage the Japanese army to fight, and hand-slipped bombs dug out of the school ditch, which were reminiscent of the horrors of the Shanghai war at that time. On the west side, there were many photos of the school being damaged, with the title (A View of Jinan After the War). Comparing the various destroyed and messy situations in the film with the currently repaired ones, we cannot help but feel indignant at the astonishing destructive power of the war.

The school's girls' dormitory was also open for two days at the same time. Many female guests visited. According to the person in charge of the school, tomorrow there will be additions of calligraphy and painting by celebrities and stone inscriptions collected by a professor.

All Circles Held a Grand Meeting Yesterday to Commemorate the Premier's Birthday

More than 500 Representatives from All Circles Attended

Yesterday morning, all circles in this city held a grand meeting to commemorate Sun Yat-sen's birthday at the auditorium of the Ximen Municipal Party Headquarters. More than 500 representatives from various agencies attended.

▲The Meeting Place was Decorated The words "The Municipal Circles Hold a Grand Meeting to Commemorate the Premier's Birthday" hung high at the front of the gate. The Party and National Flags and the Premier's portrait were hung in the meeting place. The meeting order was on the east side, the meeting slogan was on the west side, and all kinds of slogans were eye-catching, such as "Dr. Sun Yat-sen is a tough, noble, and great revolutionary mentor," "To commemorate the Premier, we must eliminate the Red bandits and stabilize society," "To commemorate the Premier, we must make the greatest determination to fight for national survival," and "The Premier's birthday is a day to commemorate the development of the Chinese nation's new life."

▲Opening of the Meeting At 9:00 AM, the bell rang to start the meeting. Tao Baichuan, Chairman of the Municipal Party Headquarters, performed the ceremony as usual. First, the chairman reported on the significance of commemorating the Premier and his life's revolutionary history and achievements. He briefly stated that we commemorate the Premier to inherit the Premier's spirit and complete the revolutionary mission. During this period of national crisis, we should especially uphold the Premier's fearless spirit, unite as one, and go to the national crisis together. He especially hoped that the people in the rear would ㈠ try to raise funds to help the Northeast Volunteer Army, which is fighting for the glory of the nation, and ㈡ strictly resist Japanese goods. He shouted slogans and did not disperse until 11:00 AM.

Yesterday's Opening of the Ancient Artifacts Museum at Baosheng Temple in Jiaozhi

A large crowd attended the opening ceremony yesterday morning.

Three people tragically drowned in a boat capsizing accident between Suzhou and Kunshan.

The Ancient Artifacts Museum at Baosheng Temple in Jiaozhi Town, under the jurisdiction of Kunshan and Wu Counties in Jiangsu Province, was planned and constructed by the Committee for the Preservation of Tang Sculptures in Jiaozhi of the Ministry of Education. The project took three years to complete and finally opened yesterday. Many people from Beijing, Shanghai, Zhenjiang, Suzhou, and other places attended the opening ceremony, creating a grand spectacle. However, a small passenger boat carrying passengers from Suzhou to Jiaozhi capsized en route. Three passengers tragically drowned, which is truly unfortunate. Details of the incident are as follows:

▲ Grand Opening Scene

Attendees at yesterday's ceremony included Central Committee member Cai Yuanpei and his wife, former Minister of Railways Ye Gongchuo, Jiangsu Provincial Government Chairman Gu Zhutong's representative Dong Xiu, Jiangsu Provincial Finance Director Shu Shiwen, Central Research Institute Vice President Yang Xingfo, Jiangsu Provincial Party Committee members, Jiangsu Higher Court President Lin Biao, Kunshan County Magistrate Cheng Ruji, and about 500 guests from various locations. Those traveling from Shanghai took the 7:00 AM express train from the North Station to Kunshan, then boarded a special boat prepared by the Ancient Artifacts Museum Board of Directors at the Zhengyang Bridge Liutong Steamboat Wharf for Jiaozhi, arriving at 11:30 AM. Those traveling from Nanjing, Zhenjiang, and Suzhou boarded a special boat prepared by the association at the Guangji Bridge pier outside the Changmen Gate in Suzhou at 7:00 AM, heading to Jiaozhi. Along the way, water patrol teams had patrol boats stationed along the Wusong River, and the Public Security Bureau's police patrol team had sentries stationed on land for patrol and security. The opening ceremony was held at noon, with the following program: (1) Opening the door, (2) Opening the meeting, (3) All stand at attention and bow three times to the Party flag, the national flag, and the portrait of the Premier, (4) Silent tribute, (5) Chairman's speech, (6) Report on the process, (7) Guest speeches, (8) Photography, (9) Adjournment. Chairman Cai Yuanpei rang the bell to open the meeting. The crowd gathered at the gate of Baosheng Temple, and the national flag was raised. Mrs. Zhou, Cai Yuanpei's wife, performed the opening ceremony, inserting the key into the lock, unlocking the door, and the crowd entered the temple to begin the meeting.

▲ Chairman's Speech

Chairman Cai Yuanpei delivered a speech, saying:

"Today is the opening day of the Ancient Artifacts Museum at Baosheng Temple in Jiaozhi. I am very grateful for the presence of local officials and guests from all walks of life. Today is the Premier's birthday. In his lectures on nationalism, the Premier strongly stated that we have the ability to restore our national heritage. This ability lies not only in scientific inventions and applications but also in artistic creation and documentation. Holding the completion of this Ancient Artifacts Museum on the Premier's birthday signifies that we are doing our part to restore our inherent capabilities, which is a meaningful act. Statues are a unique art form in our country. Among the ancient works that survive to this day, the Song Dynasty Arhat statues in Lingyan, Shandong, and the Yuan Dynasty Buddhist and Taoist statues sculpted by Liu Lan in Beiping are the most famous. However, Tang statues are still lacking. (I do not know if there are any surviving objects in Shaanxi, Shanxi, Henan, or Shandong). The discovery of the Tang Dynasty Arhat statues in Baosheng Temple in Jiaozhi shocked the art world in our country. According to legend, Baosheng Temple was founded during the Xiao Liang Dynasty, but its origins are difficult to trace. The sculptures on the walls and the eighteen Arhats are detailed in the records as sculpted by Yang Huizhi of the Tang Dynasty. Huizhi was originally a painter who was as famous as Wu Daozi during the Tang Dynasty. Because he did not want to compete with Wu, he turned to sculpture. Whether the sculptures in Baosheng Temple were actually created by Yang Huizhi is not definitively proven outside of historical records. However, the Kunshan Zhi (Kunshan Gazetteer) details the fact that Yang Huizhi sculpted statues at Huiju Temple in Yufeng, so it is possible that Baosheng Temple, which is not far away, was also sculpted by Huizhi. Mr. Gu Jiegang first noticed these statues, announced them to the public, and aroused the interest of people at home and abroad. I once proposed to raise funds for their preservation but did not implement it in time, and the main hall was destroyed. Of the sculptures on the walls, those on the east, west, and north sides, only the east side remains. Including the Arhat statues that had been dismantled and stored, only nine remain. Concerned that all would be destroyed, my colleagues reported to Mr. Cai Zimin, taking photos (Li Zunyong, photographer)

and agreed on a plan to properly preserve them. A new building should be built to cover the relics, the old fragments should be mounted on the new walls, and the Arhat statues should also be installed. When I was in charge of the University Council, I proposed allocating 10,000 yuan for this purpose. Subsequently, the provincial government agreed to allocate 3,000 yuan, and philanthropists raised more than 10,000 yuan. The Ministry of Education formed a committee to oversee the project, and Yuanpei, Ye Gongchuo, Chen Qubing, Ma Xulun, Chen Wanli, Chen Jianxiu, and Jin Jiafeng were elected as standing committee members. After three years of operation, it has finally been completed today. This is indeed a matter of celebration for the art and archeological community in our country. Not only can the works of famous Tang Dynasty masters be extended in life, but also the true image of the art of that time can be seen, and the interest and clues of research can be aroused. In this era, this must be regarded as a small contribution. Moreover, Baosheng Temple is a famous ancient temple, and the architecture of its main hall was confirmed to be from the Song Dynasty. Unfortunately, it has collapsed. Now, we can only collect its old materials and put together two dougong brackets to preserve its form. We have also tried our best to collect the ancient objects in the temple for reference. Any imperfections are hoped to be pointed out. Jiaozhi is located in a remote rural area, and we are particularly ashamed of our inadequate hospitality to the guests. We hope you will forgive us."

▲ Ye's Report

Next, Ye Gongchuo reported on the restoration process, briefly stating that the restoration of the Tang Dynasty sculptures at Baosheng Temple began in November of the 18th year and has taken three years. The progress seemed rather slow because construction could not be carried out in the winter. Furthermore, this spring, Zhu Tianle died tragically in a boat accident.

Restoration was also halted for several months due to the war. Various tasks could not be carried out simultaneously. For example, sculpture walls could not be installed during the construction of the walls, and sculpture installation could not be arranged before the house was painted. Furthermore, those in charge could not be stationed here permanently, and the project could not fully meet the pre-determined requirements. Often, dismantling and rebuilding were required, or photos were sent to Shanghai to determine what to do. Therefore, it has taken until today to complete. The progress should be briefly reported as follows: (1) The construction project fully complied with the decisions of the Standing Committee. The wall behind the sculptures was entirely built with cement to ensure solidity. The museum door was changed to iron. Two flower beds were built in the courtyard to display iron bells and Tang Dynasty sutra pillars, and stone roads were paved around the perimeter, which was an increase from the original plan but did not exceed the budget. The contractor was Yao Xinji, who had built the mausoleum for Sun Yat-sen. This spring, part of the project remained unfinished, and he did not want to continue. Therefore, engineer Shi Jiagan introduced another construction company to complete the project. The payment for labor and materials was 2,000 yuan, but only 1,100 yuan was paid, with the remainder being a donation, which is deeply appreciated. (2) The sculpture repair section was the responsibility of architects Jiang Xiao'e and Hua Tianyou. The Arhats originally sculpted by Yang Huizhi were arranged on three sides of the main hall. After the hall collapsed, they were surrounded by walls. The first step was to carefully dismantle and move the enclosure walls and sculpture walls, which took more than twenty days. After the three-section clay wall was built in the back, it was found that the sculptures were old and loose, making it difficult to install them firmly. After several discussions, iron feet were installed on the wall. The original sculpture wall was badly damaged, and Mr. Jiang Xiao'e repaired it, restoring the shape and color to their original state. Of the original eighteen Arhat statues, only two were perfect and undamaged, and four were incomplete. In order to preserve the true appearance of ancient art, they were not repaired. The arrangement of the nine Arhats and the configuration of the sculpture wall were based on old photographs. (3) Economically, the Ministry of Education allocated 10,000 yuan, the Jiangsu Provincial Government allocated 3,000 yuan, and donations totaled more than 10,160 yuan, plus more than 500 yuan in interest, for a total income of more than 23,700 yuan. In terms of expenses, engineers Fan Wenzhao and Shi Jiagan, sculptors Jiang Xiao'e and Hua Tianyou, and accounting director Jin Zongcheng all performed their duties free of charge, and I also managed the paperwork. Therefore, although the administrative expenses lasted for three years, they were less than 1,000 yuan. The rest was used for construction costs of 14,500 yuan, sculpture repair costs of nearly 4,000 yuan, and other items of about 5,000 yuan. The two offsets are still less than 1,400 yuan. (4) Jin Gang Hall in front of the museum has now been verified by archeologists, part of which is Song and Yuan Dynasty architecture. It is also of great value for preservation. There must be many other ancient artifacts of Baosheng Temple that have been lost, and attention should be paid to collecting them. I hope everyone will actively contribute to see the completion soon, etc. Finally, speeches were given by Dong Gejia, Director of the Construction Department of the Jiangsu Provincial Government and Director of the Ancient Artifacts Museum, and Yuan Ying, Chairman of the Chinese Buddhist Association. Photos were taken, and the meeting adjourned.

▲ A Glimpse of the Ancient Artifacts

The Ancient Artifacts Museum is located on the original site of the main hall of Baosheng Temple, west of Jiaozhi Town. The new building has three bays and is surrounded by a low wall. Inside the museum, the front is the nine Arhats sculpted by Yang and the repaired sculpture wall. Next to it are the remnants of the beams, ridges, dragon heads, and owl horns of the original temple's main hall, as well as an ancient stone tablet. In the right front corner against the wall stands a tablet with an inscription by Cai Yuanpei and calligraphy by Ma Xulun, recording the preservation of the Tang sculptures. There are two flower beds in the courtyard, an ancient bell in the east, and a Tang Dynasty stone sutra pillar in the west. In front of it is the Jin Gang Hall, which is on the verge of collapse. There is a large Buddha statue in the middle, which is dilapidated. To the right of the temple is the gate to Duck Pond, where Mr. Lu Guimeng studied. He was also buried here after his death.

▲ Boat Capsizing Incident

During yesterday's opening ceremony, one thing was quite unfortunate. At about 11:00 AM, the Yuanxing, a boat carrying passengers from Suzhou to Jiaozhi, suddenly capsized midway. The Yuanxing was a small diesel boat with a total of fourteen people on board, including four water patrol team members, Suzhou writer Zhu Liangren and his son Shilong, Shanghai News Agency special reporter Fu Ziwen, and reporters from Suzhou and other places. The Yuanxing, Zhizhong, and other three boats were connected by a cable in a straight line. The Yuanxing was in the middle. At that time, the three boats were moving forward. The front wheel was too fast, and the rear wheel was slower. When turning, the cable suddenly turned sideways, and the Yuanxing capsized immediately. At that time, the wind was piercing, and the boat windows were closed, causing the Zhu family and Fu to drown. Others were rescued by patrol boats and sent to Suzhou for treatment. Zhu used to teach at Dongda and other schools and was 68 years old. His son, Shilong, is currently a teacher at the Cheng Lie Physical Education School in Suzhou. Fu had just returned to Suzhou the day before, representing Suzhou archeologist Jin Songcen to Jiaozhi. Unexpectedly, he also tragically drowned yesterday.

According to Suzhou news, there was a special boat from Suzhou to attend the Tang Dynasty Sculpture Opening Ceremony in Jiaozhi yesterday. The ships were Yuanxing, Xinxin, and Zhizhong steamboats from the Third District of the Water Public Security Bureau, and Anjing patrol ship. The Yuanxing, Xinxin and Zhizhong three steamboats were connected with fierce ropes, running in a line. Xinxin was in the front, Yuanxing was the second, and Zhizhong was at the end. When sailing, because Anjing's speed was very fast, and the three steamboats were lagging far behind, so they also opened up the speed. When they arrived at San Shuang Banqiao, fourteen miles away from Jiaozhi, because the river port there was narrow, and there was a stone bridge, when turning, the central Yuanxing steamboat suddenly capsized due to front and rear squeezing. There were fourteen passengers on board, all of them fell into the water. Those who drowned on the spot were Zhu Liangren and Zhu Tianlu fathers and son (Zhu Tianlu, 30 years old, Suzhou people, now the director of Cheng Lie Physical Education School, ) and Fu Ziwen from No. 11, Xizhi Jialong, Yangyu Lane. All the others were rescued with only minor injuries. Now the dead and the passengers who fell into the river have been transported back to Suzhou by Zhizhong steamboat, and the injured in the water included Suzhou reporters Xia Youwen, Hong Xiaohong, Lv Lv, and Feng Qiunong, a cadre of the County Chamber of Commerce.

▲ Yang Huizhi Examination

Yang Huizhi, the sculptor of the Baosheng Temple statues, was from the Kaiyuan period of the Tang Dynasty. He studied painting with Wu Daozi, Liang Zhang Sengyao, and Hua Fa. Later, Yang focused on sculpture and made rapid progress. His work and Wu Daozi's painting were equally important at the time. There was a saying at the time that "Daozi's painting and Huizhi's sculpture capture the divine brushstrokes of Sengyao." Yang's works were numerous. According to records, there is the Jade Emperor statue in the Taihua Temple in Changle Township, Jingzhao, the Buddha statue in the Jingshi Courtyard of Anle Temple in Haozhou, the Thousand Buddhas, the door gods behind the three gates of the Eastern Sutra Library, the Vimalakirti statue in the hall, the five hundred Arhats on the three gates of Guangai Temple in Luoyang, and Mount Lengjia in Shangaoyuan, all of which are extremely miraculous. During the Huang Chao Rebellion, all the temples in Jingluo were burned to the ground without exception. Only Yang's sculptures survived. In addition, the sculpture wall of Fuyan Temple on Mount Lishan in Linzi County, Shaanxi, and the Bishamonten statue and the two attendant girls of Huiju Temple in Kunshan are also works of Yang. In Jingzhao, Yang was said to have sculpted a statue for the actor Liubei Pavilion. After the statue was completed, it was placed against a wall in the street. People on the road, seeing its back, thought that Liubei Pavilion was traveling and competed to exchange greetings. The statue's divinity is conceivable.

Permanently Eliminating Economic Ties

Certificates for Not Buying or Selling Inferior Goods to be Issued Today
